               <div class="post-content rich-text-styled" id="rgw11_59d3942cb4377"> 
                <h1 class="topic-post-title"> How do you find semantic similarities between two or more different words? </h1> 
                <div class="topic-post-text"> 
                 <p>Given some words, how can we find relatedness between words?</p> 
                 <p>Given a word with two or more meaning in different context for example ;apple (company,laptop,fruit) ,soap(shampoo,SOAP protocol,serial soap )etc . I would like to select a word which is related to another using user interest.</p> 
                 <p>If user is interested in computer, I would like to select apple company, laptops and reject apple as fruit. Similarly in case of soap i want SOAP as a protocol to be selected.</p> 
                 <p>Is there a way to find semantic relatedness between words as required.</p> 
                 <p>note : for disambiguation of words i am using DBpedia.</p> 
                </div> 
               </div>
              </div>
             </div> 
            </div>

              <li id="rgw59_59d3942cb4377" class="comment"> 
               <div class="actions-secondary rf"> 
               </div> 
               <div class="comment-image"> 
                <a href="profile/Amit_Sheth"> <img width="30" height="30" src="https://i1.rgstatic.net/ii/profile.image/AS%3A272383281987590%401441952643673_m/Amit_Sheth.jpg" title="Amit Sheth" alt="Amit Sheth"> </a> 
               </div> 
               <div class="comment-content"> 
                <div class="comment-author"> 
                 <strong><a href="profile/Amit_Sheth">Amit Sheth</a></strong> · Wright State University 
                </div> 
                <div class="js-content"> 
                 <div id="rgw60_59d3942cb4377" class="react-container">
                  <div class="js-backend-rendered" data-reactroot="" data-reactid="1" data-react-checksum="1976307209">
                   <div id="rgw61_59d3942cb4377" class="post-edit-content comment-body topic-post-text rich-text-styled"> 
                    <p>Before a good answer can be given, try to decide your definition of similarity. How are two terms or words related? Exact similarity or synonymy is better defined and hence easier to computer. But what about similarity in one&nbsp;context and not in other? [Is DBPedia the right basis for context and hence disambiguation?] What about partial similarity or relatedness? What is the model in which you can consider matching and mapping? &nbsp;To give you an analogy, see a relatively broader model of similarity&nbsp;called "semantic proximity" in&nbsp;<a href="https://www.researchgate.net/deref/http%3A%2F%2Fdl.acm.org%2Fcitation.cfm%3Fid%3D765855" rel="noopener" target="_blank">http://dl.acm.org/citation.cfm?id=765855</a> . It requires you to consider the domain and context, the model of representation, whether you are limited to schema level information or are also looking at instances.</p> 
                    <p>Now you may need to define the model for your need (which is not the database as in the reference above). There is a rich literature on semantic relationships...may want to check it.</p> 
                    <p>On the other hand, current view on ontology alignment (and the benchmarks used for a popular evaluation referred to OAEI) offers a very narrow types of similarities/relationships, and hence has a limited value.</p> 
                   </div>
                  </div>
                 </div> 
                </div>

                  <div class="js-backend-rendered" data-reactroot="" data-reactid="1" data-react-checksum="1438374314">
                   <div id="rgw66_59d3942cb4377" class="post-edit-content comment-body topic-post-text rich-text-styled"> 
                    <p>Maybe our paper on "Analysis of word co-occurrence in human literature for supporting semantic correspondence discovery" can help.</p> 
                    <p>Regards, Mario</p> 
                    <div id="rgw67_59d3942cb4377" class="post-attachments-list"> 
                     <ul class="publication-attachments-list attachments-category"> 
                      <li class="c-list-item li-publication  " id="rgw68_59d3942cb4377"> 
                       <div class="indent-left"> 
                        <div id="rgw69_59d3942cb4377" class="js-publication-item-fulltext fulltext-thumb"> 
                         <a class="publication-preview preview-not-available ga-publication-viewer-not-available js-publication-item-fulltext-content" href="publication/265729707_Analysis_of_word_co-occurrence_in_human_literature_for_supporting_semantic_correspondence_discovery"> </a> 
                        </div> 
                       </div> 
                       <div class="indent-right"> 
                       </div> 
                       <div style="margin-top: -2px"> 
                        <h5 class="pub-type-and-title"> <span class="publication-type">Conference Paper:</span> <a class="js-publication-title-link ga-publication-item" href="publication/265729707_Analysis_of_word_co-occurrence_in_human_literature_for_supporting_semantic_correspondence_discovery?ev=post"> <span class="publication-title js-publication-title">Analysis of word co-occurrence in human literature for supporting semantic correspondence discovery</span> </a> </h5> 
                       </div> 
                       <div class="authors"> 
                        <a href="profile/Jorge_Martinez-Gil" class="authors js-author-name ga-publications-authors"> Jorge Martinez-Gil </a> · 
                        <a href="profile/Mario_Pichler" class="authors js-author-name ga-publications-authors"> Mario Pichler </a> 
                       </div> 
                       <div class="abstract"> 
                        <span class="shorten"> <a href="javascript:" class="js-toggle-abstract">[Show abstract]</a> </span> 
                        <span class="full"> <a href="javascript:" class="js-toggle-abstract">[Hide abstract]</a> <strong>ABSTRACT:</strong> Semantic similarity measurement aims to determine the likeness between two text expressions that use different lexicographies for representing the same real object or idea. In this work, we describe the way to exploit broad cultural trends for identifying semantic similarity. This is possible through the quantitative analysis of a vast digital book collection representing the digested history of humanity. Our research work has revealed that appropriately analyzing the co-occurrence of words in some periods of human literature can help us to determine the semantic similarity between these words by means of computers with a high degree of accuracy. </span> 
                       </div> 
                       <div class="publication-meta">
                         Conference Paper · Sep 2014 
                       </div> </li> 
                     </ul> 
                    </div> 
                   </div>
                  </div>
                 </div> 
                </div>

                <a href="profile/Efstratios_Kontopoulos"> <img width="30" height="30" src="https://i1.rgstatic.net/ii/profile.image/AS%3A320708691857409%401453474318566_m/Efstratios_Kontopoulos.jpg" title="Efstratios Kontopoulos" alt="Efstratios Kontopoulos"> </a>

               <div class="comment-content"> 
                <div class="comment-author"> 
                 <strong><a href="profile/Efstratios_Kontopoulos">Efstratios Kontopoulos</a></strong> · The Centre for Research and Technology, Hellas 
                </div> 
                <div class="js-content"> 
                 <div id="rgw78_59d3942cb4377" class="react-container">
                  <div class="js-backend-rendered" data-reactroot="" data-reactid="1" data-react-checksum="1135202748">
                   <div id="rgw79_59d3942cb4377" class="post-edit-content comment-body topic-post-text rich-text-styled"> 
                    <p>Hi there, in recent work of ours (see attachment) we have also used ws4j, suggested by Kazem above.</p> 
                    <div id="rgw80_59d3942cb4377" class="post-attachments-list"> 
                     <ul class="publication-attachments-list attachments-category"> 
                      <li class="c-list-item li-publication  " id="rgw81_59d3942cb4377"> 
                       <div class="indent-left"> 
                        <div id="rgw82_59d3942cb4377" class="js-publication-item-fulltext fulltext-thumb"> 
                         <a class="publication-preview ga-publication-viewer js-publication-item-fulltext-content" href="publication/272027157_Monitoring_Term_Drift_Based_on_Semantic_Consistency_in_an_Evolving_Vector_Field"> </a> 
                         <div class="preview-source-info"> 
                          <a class="details js-show-source ga-source-url" href="profile/Efstratios_Kontopoulos" rel="noopener">Source</a> 
                          <div class="tooltip-content" style="display: none">
                            Available from: Efstratios Kontopoulos 
                          </div> 
                         </div> 
                        </div> 
                       </div> 
                       <div class="indent-right"> 
                       </div> 
                       <div style="margin-top: -2px"> 
                        <h5 class="pub-type-and-title"> <span class="publication-type">Conference Paper:</span> <a class="js-publication-title-link ga-publication-item" href="publication/272027157_Monitoring_Term_Drift_Based_on_Semantic_Consistency_in_an_Evolving_Vector_Field?ev=post"> <span class="publication-title js-publication-title">Monitoring Term Drift Based on Semantic Consistency in an Evolving Vector Field</span> </a> </h5> 
                       </div> 
                       <div class="authors"> 
                        <a href="profile/Peter_Wittek" class="authors js-author-name ga-publications-authors"> Peter Wittek </a> · 
                        <a href="profile/Sandor_Daranyi" class="authors js-author-name ga-publications-authors"> Sándor Darányi </a> · 
                        <a href="profile/Efstratios_Kontopoulos" class="authors js-author-name ga-publications-authors"> Efstratios Kontopoulos </a> · 
                        <span class="authors js-author-name ga-publications-authors"> [...] </span> · 
                        <a href="profile/Ioannis_Kompatsiaris" class="authors js-author-name ga-publications-authors"> Ioannis Kompatsiaris </a> 
                       </div> 
                       <div class="abstract"> 
                        <span class="shorten"> <a href="javascript:" class="js-toggle-abstract">[Show abstract]</a> </span> 
                        <span class="full"> <a href="javascript:" class="js-toggle-abstract">[Hide abstract]</a> <strong>ABSTRACT:</strong> Based on the Aristotelian concept of potentiality vs. actuality allowing for the study of energy and dynamics in language, we propose a field approach to lexical analysis. Falling back on the distributional hypothesis to statistically model word meaning, we used evolving fields as a metaphor to express time-dependent changes in a vector space model by a combination of random indexing and evolving self-organizing maps (ESOM). To monitor semantic drifts within the observation period, an experiment was carried out on the term space of a collection of 12.8 million Amazon book reviews. For evaluation, the semantic consistency of ESOM term clusters was compared with their respective neighbourhoods in WordNet, and contrasted with distances among term vectors by random indexing. We found that at 0.05 level of significance, the terms in the clusters showed a high level of semantic consistency. Tracking the drift of distributional patterns in the term space across time periods, we found that consistency decreased, but not at a statistically significant level. Our method is highly scalable, with interpretations in philosophy. </span> 
                       </div> 
                       <div class="publication-meta">
                         Full-text available · Conference Paper · Jul 2015 
                       </div>

                        </div> 
                       </div> </li>

               <div class="actions-secondary rf">

               <div class="comment-image"> 
                <a href="profile/James_OShea2"> <img width="30" height="30" src="https://i1.rgstatic.net/ii/profile.image/AS%3A273791557304345%401442288402640_m/James_OShea2.jpg" title="James Dominic O'Shea" alt="James Dominic O'Shea"> </a> 
               </div> 
               <div class="comment-content"> 
                <div class="comment-author"> 
                 <strong><a href="profile/James_OShea2">James Dominic O'Shea</a></strong> · Manchester Metropolitan University 
                </div> 
                <div class="js-content"> 
                 <div id="rgw86_59d3942cb4377" class="react-container">
                  <div class="js-backend-rendered" data-reactroot="" data-reactid="1" data-react-checksum="-2078209728">
                   <div id="rgw87_59d3942cb4377" class="post-edit-content comment-body topic-post-text rich-text-styled"> 
                    <p>The first algorithm specifically designed for Short Text Semantic Similarity can be found here:</p> 
                    <p><a href="https://www.researchgate.net/deref/http%3A%2F%2Fwww.aaai.org%2FPapers%2FFLAIRS%2F2004%2FFlairs04-139.pdf" rel="noopener" target="_blank">http://www.aaai.org/Papers/FLAIRS/2004/Flairs04-139.pdf</a></p> 
                    <p>With a more extensive treatment here:</p> 
                    <p><a href="https://www.researchgate.net/deref/http%3A%2F%2Fants.iis.sinica.edu.tw%2F3BkMJ9lTeWXTSrrvNoKNFDxRm3zFwRR%2F55%2FSentence%2520Similarity%2520Based%2520on%2520Semantic%2520Nets%2520and%2520corpus%2520statistics.pdf" rel="noopener" target="_blank">http://ants.iis.sinica.edu.tw/3BkMJ9lTeWXTSrrvNoKNFDxRm3zFwRR/55/Sentence%20Similarity%20Based%20on%20Semantic%20Nets%20and%20corpus%20statistics.pdf</a></p> 
                    <p>This paper should give you some further insight on interpreting performance of Short Text Semantic Similarity measures:</p> 
                    <p><a href="https://www.researchgate.net/publication/262411640_A_new_benchmark_dataset_with_production_methodology_for_short_text_semantic_similarity_algorithms">https://www.researchgate.net/publication/262411640_A_new_benchmark_dataset_with_production_methodology_for_short_text_semantic_similarity_algorithms</a></p> 
                    <p>"Short Texts" are of approximately sentence length. The *Sem group set a challenge on "Semantic Text Similarity" I analysed their datasets and found the text lengths to vary from 3 to over 60 words. You can find them at:</p> 
                    <p><a href="https://www.researchgate.net/deref/http%3A%2F%2Falt.qcri.org%2Fsemeval2015%2Ftask2%2F" rel="noopener" target="_blank">http://alt.qcri.org/semeval2015/task2/</a></p> 
                    <div id="rgw88_59d3942cb4377" class="post-attachments-list"> 
                     <ul class="publication-attachments-list attachments-category"> 
                      <li class="c-list-item li-publication  " id="rgw89_59d3942cb4377"> 
                       <div class="indent-left"> 
                        <div id="rgw90_59d3942cb4377" class="js-publication-item-fulltext fulltext-thumb"> 
                         <a class="publication-preview ga-publication-viewer js-publication-item-fulltext-content" href="publication/262411640_A_new_benchmark_dataset_with_production_methodology_for_short_text_semantic_similarity_algorithms"> </a> 
                         <div class="preview-source-info"> 
                          <a class="details js-show-source ga-source-url" href="profile/James_OShea2" rel="noopener">Source</a> 
                          <div class="tooltip-content" style="display: none">
                            Available from: James Dominic O'Shea 
                          </div> 
                         </div> 
                        </div> 
                       </div> 
                       <div class="indent-right"> 
                       </div> 
                       <div style="margin-top: -2px"> 
                        <h5 class="pub-type-and-title"> <span class="publication-type">Article:</span> <a class="js-publication-title-link ga-publication-item" href="publication/262411640_A_new_benchmark_dataset_with_production_methodology_for_short_text_semantic_similarity_algorithms?ev=post"> <span class="publication-title js-publication-title">A new benchmark dataset with production methodology for short text semantic similarity algorithms</span> </a> </h5> 
                       </div> 
                       <div class="authors"> 
                        <a href="profile/James_OShea2" class="authors js-author-name ga-publications-authors"> James O'shea </a> · 
                        <a href="scientific-contributions/7685146_Zuhair_Bandar" class="authors js-author-name ga-publications-authors"> Zuhair Bandar </a> · 
                        <a href="profile/Keeley_Crockett" class="authors js-author-name ga-publications-authors"> Keeley Crockett </a> 
                       </div> 
                       <div class="abstract"> 
                        <span class="shorten"> <a href="javascript:" class="js-toggle-abstract">[Show abstract]</a> </span> 
                        <span class="full"> <a href="javascript:" class="js-toggle-abstract">[Hide abstract]</a> <strong>ABSTRACT:</strong> This research presents a new benchmark dataset for evaluating Short Text Semantic Similarity (STSS) measurement algorithms and the methodology used for its creation. The power of the dataset is evaluated by using it to compare two established algorithms, STASIS and Latent Semantic Analysis. This dataset focuses on measures for use in Conversational Agents; other potential applications include email processing and data mining of social networks. Such applications involve integrating the STSS algorithm in a complex system, but STSS algorithms must be evaluated in their own right and compared with others for their effectiveness before systems integration. Semantic similarity is an artifact of human perception; therefore its evaluation is inherently empirical and requires benchmark datasets derived from human similarity ratings. The new dataset of 64 sentence pairs, STSS-131, has been designed to meet these requirements drawing on a range of resources from traditional grammar to cognitive neuroscience. The human ratings are obtained from a set of trials using new and improved experimental methods, with validated measures and statistics. The results illustrate the increased challenge and the potential longevity of the STSS-131 dataset as the Gold Standard for future STSS algorithm evaluation. </span> 
                       </div> 
                       <div class="publication-meta">
                         Full-text available · Article · Dec 2013 · ACM Transactions on Speech and Language Processing 
                       </div>

               <div class="comment-content">

                <div class="js-content">

                   <div id="rgw95_59d3942cb4377" class="post-edit-content comment-body topic-post-text rich-text-styled"> 
                    <p>use a python-based implementation of different similarity measures, such&nbsp;Dekang Lins proximity based thesaurus (Lin, 1998). For reference, have a look at following work:</p> 
                    <p><a href="https://www.researchgate.net/publication/273727879_Medical_opinion_lexicon_an_incremental_model_for_mining_health_reviews">https://www.researchgate.net/publication/273727879_Medical_opinion_lexicon_an_incremental_model_for_mining_health_reviews</a></p> 
                    <div id="rgw96_59d3942cb4377" class="post-attachments-list"> 
                     <ul class="publication-attachments-list attachments-category"> 
                      <li class="c-list-item li-publication  " id="rgw97_59d3942cb4377"> 
                       <div class="indent-left"> 
                        <div id="rgw98_59d3942cb4377" class="js-publication-item-fulltext fulltext-thumb"> 
                         <a class="publication-preview ga-publication-viewer js-publication-item-fulltext-content" href="publication/273727879_Medical_opinion_lexicon_An_incremental_model_for_mining_health_reviews"> </a> 
                         <div class="preview-source-info"> 
                          <a class="details js-show-source ga-source-url" href="profile/Dr_Muhammad_Asghar" rel="noopener">Source</a> 
                          <div class="tooltip-content" style="display: none">
                            Available from: Dr. Muhammad Zubair Asghar 
                          </div> 
                         </div> 
                        </div> 
                       </div> 
                       <div class="indent-right"> 
                       </div> 
                       <div style="margin-top: -2px"> 
                        <h5 class="pub-type-and-title"> <span class="publication-type">Article:</span> <a class="js-publication-title-link ga-publication-item" href="publication/273727879_Medical_opinion_lexicon_An_incremental_model_for_mining_health_reviews?ev=post"> <span class="publication-title js-publication-title">Medical opinion lexicon: An incremental model for mining health reviews</span> </a> </h5> 
                       </div> 
                       <div class="authors"> 
                        <a href="profile/Dr_Muhammad_Asghar" class="authors js-author-name ga-publications-authors"> Muhammad Zubair Asghar </a> · 
                        <a href="profile/Aurangzeb_Khan10" class="authors js-author-name ga-publications-authors"> Aurangzeb Khan </a> · 
                        <a href="scientific-contributions/2069543267_Fazal_Masud_Kundi" class="authors js-author-name ga-publications-authors"> Fazal Masud Kundi </a> · 
                        <span class="authors js-author-name ga-publications-authors"> [...] </span> · 
                        <a href="scientific-contributions/2069535876_Irfan_Ullah_Nawaz" class="authors js-author-name ga-publications-authors"> Irfan Ullah Nawaz </a> 
                       </div> 
                       <div class="abstract"> 
                        <span class="shorten"> <a href="javascript:" class="js-toggle-abstract">[Show abstract]</a> </span> 
                        <span class="full"> <a href="javascript:" class="js-toggle-abstract">[Hide abstract]</a> <strong>ABSTRACT:</strong> Opinion mining concentrates on retrieving opinions of online users about a service, product, and policy. In this paper, we propose a medical opinion lexicon for mining health reviews available on different health forums. The proposed technique is based on the incremental modal and corpus of health reviews by creating medical polarity lexicon for medical terms. In each increment, vocabulary of lexicon is enhanced systematically, polarity score with each word is attached, and finally, resulting lexicon is filtered from unnecessary words by using word sense disambiguation techniques. The comparative results show the efficiency of proposed method and it outperforms the existing approaches. The proposed approach achieves an accuracy of 82% on training corpus and 78% on testing corpus of health reviews. </span> 
                       </div> 
                       <div class="publication-meta">
                         Full-text available · Article · Jan 2014 
                       </div>

Falling back on the distributional hypothesis to\nstatistically model word meaning, we used evolving fields as a metaphor to\nexpress time-dependent changes in a vector space model by a combination of\nrandom indexing and evolving self-organizing maps (ESOM). To monitor semantic\ndrifts within the observation period, an experiment was carried out on the term\nspace of a collection of 12.8 million Amazon book reviews. measurement algorithms and the methodology used for its creation. The power of the dataset is evaluated by using it to compare two established algorithms, STASIS and Latent Semantic Analysis. This dataset focuses on measures for use in Conversational Agents; other potential applications include email processing and data mining of social networks. Such applications involve integrating the STSS algorithm in a complex system, but STSS algorithms must be evaluated in their own right and compared with others for their effectiveness before systems integration. Semantic similarity is an artifact of human perception; therefore its evaluation is inherently empirical and requires benchmark datasets derived from human similarity ratings. The new dataset of 64 sentence pairs, STSS-131, has been designed to meet these requirements drawing on a range of resources from traditional grammar to cognitive neuroscience. The human ratings are obtained from a set of trials using new and improved experimental methods, with validated measures and statistics. The results illustrate the increased challenge and the potential longevity of the STSS-131 dataset as the Gold Standard for future STSS algorithm In this paper, we propose a medical opinion lexicon for mining health reviews available on different health forums. The proposed technique is based on the incremental modal and corpus of health reviews by creating medical polarity lexicon for medical terms. In each increment, vocabulary of lexicon is enhanced systematically, polarity score with each word is attached, and finally, resulting lexicon is filtered from unnecessary words by using word sense disambiguation techniques. The comparative results show the efficiency of proposed method and it outperforms the existing approaches. The proposed approach achieves an accuracy of 82% on training corpus and 78% on testing corpus of health
